The Book of Common Prayer - 1559





THE TABLE AND CALENDAR

EXPRESSING THE ORDRE OF THE PSALMS AND LESSONS,

TO BEE SAID AT THE MORNING AND EVENING PRAYER

THROUGHOUT THE YEAR, EXCEPT CERTAIN PROPRE

FEASTS, AS THE RULES FOLLOWING

MORE PLAINLY DECLARE.



* * *



THE ORDER HOW THE PSALTER IS APPOINTED TO BE READ.

THE Psalter shall be read through, ones every month, and because that some Months bee longer then some other be; It is thought good, to make them even by this means.

To every month shall be appointed (as concerning this purpose) just xxx days.

And because January and March has one day above the said number, and February, which is placed between them both, hath only xxviii days, February shall borrow of either of the months (of January and March) one day, and so the Psalter, which shall be red in February, must begin the last day of January, and end the first day of March.

And where as May, July, August, October and December, hath xxxi days a piece, it is ordered that the same Psalms shall be red the haste day of the said Months, which were red the day before, so that the Psalter may begin again the first day of the next Month ensuing.

Now to know what Psalms shall be red every day, look in the Calendar, the number that is appointed for the Psalms, and then find the same number in this Table, and upon that number shall you see, what Psalms shall be said at Morning and Evening prayer.

And where the cxix Psalm, is divided into xxii porcions, and is overlong to be red at one time: it is so ordered, that, at one time, shall not be read above four or five of the said porcions, as you shall perceive to be noted in this Table following.

And here is also to be noted, that in this Table, and in all other parts of the service, where any Psalms are appointed, the nombre is expressed after the great English Bible, which from the ix Psalm, unto the cxlviii Psalm (following the division of the Hebrues) doth vary in nombres from the common Latin translacion.



* * *

* * *



THE ORDER

HOWE THE REST OF HOLY SCRIPTURE (BESIDE THE PSALTER)

IS APPOINTED TO BE READ.

THOLD Testament is appointed for the first lessons, at Morning and Evening prayer, and shall be read through, every year once, except certain books and Chapiters, which be least edifying, and might best bee spared, and therefore bee left unread.

The new Testament is appointed for the second Lessons, at Morning and Evening prayer, and shall be read over orderly every year thryse, beside the Epistles and Gospels: except the Apocalips [=Revelation], out of the which there bee only certain Lessons appointed, upon diverse proper feasts.

And to know what Lessons shall be read every day: find the day of the month in the Calendar following; and there ye shall perceive the books and Chapiters that shall be read for the Lessons, both at Morning and Evening prayer.

And here is to bee noted, that whenever there bee any proper Psalms or Lessons appointed for the Sondayes or for any feast moveable or unmovable: then the Psalms and Lessons, appointed in the calendar shall be omitted for that time.

Ye must note also that the Collect Epistle and Gospel, appointed for the Sunday shall serve al the weke after, except there fall some feast that hath his proper.

This is also to bee noted, concerning the Leap years, that the xxv day of February, which in Leap year is counted for two days, shall in those two days, alter nether Psalm nor Lesson: but the same Psalms and Lessons, which be said the first day, shall also serve for the second day.

Also, wheresoever the beginning of any Lesson, Epistle or Gospel is not expressed: there ye must begin at the beginning of the Chapiter.

And wheresoever is not expressed howe far shall be read, there shall you read to the end of the Chapiter.

* * *





A Brief Declaration

When Every Term Begins

and Ends

[After 1604, this is found at the very end of this section.]

BE it known that Easter Term begins always the eighteenth day after Easter, reckoning Easter Day for one. And ends the Monday next after Ascension Day.

Trinity Term begins always the Friday next after Trinity Sunday and ends the twenty-eighth day of June.

Michaelmas Term begins the ninth or tenth day of October and ends the twenty-eighth or twenty-ninth day of November.

Hilary Term begins the twenty-third or twenty-fourth day of January and ends the twelfth or thirteenth day of February.

In Easter Term on the Ascension Day, in Trinity Term on the Nativity of Saint John Baptist, in Michaelmas Term on the Feast of All Saints, in Hilary Term on the Feast of the Purification of our Lady, the Queen's judges of Westminster do not use to sit in judgment, nor upon any Sundays.

The following was added in 1561:



* * *



These to be observed for Holy days,

and none other.

THat is to say, All Sundays in the year. The days of the Feasts of the Circimcision of our Lord Jesus Chrsit. Of the Epiphany. Of the Purification of the blessed Virgin. Of S. Matthias the Apostle. Of the Enunciation of the blessed Virgin. Of S. Mark the Evangelist. Of S. Philip and Jacob Apostles. Of the Ascension of our Lord Jesus Christ. Of the Nativity of S. John Baptist. Of S. Peter the Apostle. Of S. James the Apostle. Of S. Bartholomew the Apostle. Of S. Matthew the Apostle. Of S. Michael the Archangel. Of S. Luke the Evangelist. Of S. Simon and Jude Apostles. Of All Saints. Of S. Andrew the Apostle. Of S. Thomas the Apostle. Of the Nativity of our Lord. Of S. Steven the Martyr. Of S. John Evangelist. Of the holy Innocents. Monday and Tuesday in Easter week. Monday and Tuesday in Whitsun week.

The Book of Common Prayer - 1559





THE TABLE AND CALENDAR

EXPRESSING THE ORDRE OF THE PSALMS AND LESSONS,

TO BEE SAID AT THE MORNING AND EVENING PRAYER

THROUGHOUT THE YEAR, EXCEPT CERTAIN PROPRE

FEASTS, AS THE RULES FOLLOWING

MORE PLAINLY DECLARE.



* * *



THE ORDER HOW THE PSALTER IS APPOINTED TO BE READ.

THE Psalter shall be read through, ones every month, and because that some Months bee longer then some other be; It is thought good, to make them even by this means.

To every month shall be appointed (as concerning this purpose) just xxx days.

And because January and March has one day above the said number, and February, which is placed between them both, hath only xxviii days, February shall borrow of either of the months (of January and March) one day, and so the Psalter, which shall be red in February, must begin the last day of January, and end the first day of March.

And where as May, July, August, October and December, hath xxxi days a piece, it is ordered that the same Psalms shall be red the haste day of the said Months, which were red the day before, so that the Psalter may begin again the first day of the next Month ensuing.

Now to know what Psalms shall be red every day, look in the Calendar, the number that is appointed for the Psalms, and then find the same number in this Table, and upon that number shall you see, what Psalms shall be said at Morning and Evening prayer.

And where the cxix Psalm, is divided into xxii porcions, and is overlong to be red at one time: it is so ordered, that, at one time, shall not be read above four or five of the said porcions, as you shall perceive to be noted in this Table following.

And here is also to be noted, that in this Table, and in all other parts of the service, where any Psalms are appointed, the nombre is expressed after the great English Bible, which from the ix Psalm, unto the cxlviii Psalm (following the division of the Hebrues) doth vary in nombres from the common Latin translacion.

* * *



THE ORDER

HOWE THE REST OF HOLY SCRIPTURE (BESIDE THE PSALTER)

IS APPOINTED TO BE READ.

THOLD Testament is appointed for the first lessons, at Morning and Evening prayer, and shall be read through, every year once, except certain books and Chapiters, which be least edifying, and might best bee spared, and therefore bee left unread.

The new Testament is appointed for the second Lessons, at Morning and Evening prayer, and shall be read over orderly every year thryse, beside the Epistles and Gospels: except the Apocalips [=Revelation], out of the which there bee only certain Lessons appointed, upon diverse proper feasts.

And to know what Lessons shall be read every day: find the day of the month in the Calendar following; and there ye shall perceive the books and Chapiters that shall be read for the Lessons, both at Morning and Evening prayer.

And here is to bee noted, that whenever there bee any proper Psalms or Lessons appointed for the Sondayes or for any feast moveable or unmovable: then the Psalms and Lessons, appointed in the calendar shall be omitted for that time.

Ye must note also that the Collect Epistle and Gospel, appointed for the Sunday shall serve al the weke after, except there fall some feast that hath his proper.

This is also to bee noted, concerning the Leap years, that the xxv day of February, which in Leap year is counted for two days, shall in those two days, alter nether Psalm nor Lesson: but the same Psalms and Lessons, which be said the first day, shall also serve for the second day.

Also, wheresoever the beginning of any Lesson, Epistle or Gospel is not expressed: there ye must begin at the beginning of the Chapiter.

And wheresoever is not expressed howe far shall be read, there shall you read to the end of the Chapiter.

* * *





A Brief Declaration

When Every Term Begins

and Ends

[After 1604, this is found at the very end of this section.]

BE it known that Easter Term begins always the eighteenth day after Easter, reckoning Easter Day for one. And ends the Monday next after Ascension Day.

Trinity Term begins always the Friday next after Trinity Sunday and ends the twenty-eighth day of June.

Michaelmas Term begins the ninth or tenth day of October and ends the twenty-eighth or twenty-ninth day of November.

Hilary Term begins the twenty-third or twenty-fourth day of January and ends the twelfth or thirteenth day of February.

In Easter Term on the Ascension Day, in Trinity Term on the Nativity of Saint John Baptist, in Michaelmas Term on the Feast of All Saints, in Hilary Term on the Feast of the Purification of our Lady, the Queen's judges of Westminster do not use to sit in judgment, nor upon any Sundays.

The following was added in 1561:



* * *



These to be observed for Holy days,

and none other.

THat is to say, All Sundays in the year. The days of the Feasts of the Circimcision of our Lord Jesus Chrsit. Of the Epiphany. Of the Purification of the blessed Virgin. Of S. Matthias the Apostle. Of the Enunciation of the blessed Virgin. Of S. Mark the Evangelist. Of S. Philip and Jacob Apostles. Of the Ascension of our Lord Jesus Christ. Of the Nativity of S. John Baptist. Of S. Peter the Apostle. Of S. James the Apostle. Of S. Bartholomew the Apostle. Of S. Matthew the Apostle. Of S. Michael the Archangel. Of S. Luke the Evangelist. Of S. Simon and Jude Apostles. Of All Saints. Of S. Andrew the Apostle. Of S. Thomas the Apostle. Of the Nativity of our Lord. Of S. Steven the Martyr. Of S. John Evangelist. Of the holy Innocents. Monday and Tuesday in Easter week. Monday and Tuesday in Whitsun week.

The Book of Common Prayer - 1559





THE TABLE AND CALENDAR

EXPRESSING THE ORDRE OF THE PSALMS AND LESSONS,

TO BEE SAID AT THE MORNING AND EVENING PRAYER

THROUGHOUT THE YEAR, EXCEPT CERTAIN PROPRE

FEASTS, AS THE RULES FOLLOWING

MORE PLAINLY DECLARE.



* * *



THE ORDER HOW THE PSALTER IS APPOINTED TO BE READ.

THE Psalter shall be read through, ones every month, and because that some Months bee longer then some other be; It is thought good, to make them even by this means.

To every month shall be appointed (as concerning this purpose) just xxx days.

And because January and March has one day above the said number, and February, which is placed between them both, hath only xxviii days, February shall borrow of either of the months (of January and March) one day, and so the Psalter, which shall be red in February, must begin the last day of January, and end the first day of March.

And where as May, July, August, October and December, hath xxxi days a piece, it is ordered that the same Psalms shall be red the haste day of the said Months, which were red the day before, so that the Psalter may begin again the first day of the next Month ensuing.

Now to know what Psalms shall be red every day, look in the Calendar, the number that is appointed for the Psalms, and then find the same number in this Table, and upon that number shall you see, what Psalms shall be said at Morning and Evening prayer.

And where the cxix Psalm, is divided into xxii porcions, and is overlong to be red at one time: it is so ordered, that, at one time, shall not be read above four or five of the said porcions, as you shall perceive to be noted in this Table following.

And here is also to be noted, that in this Table, and in all other parts of the service, where any Psalms are appointed, the nombre is expressed after the great English Bible, which from the ix Psalm, unto the cxlviii Psalm (following the division of the Hebrues) doth vary in nombres from the common Latin translacion.



* * *

* * *



THE ORDER

HOWE THE REST OF HOLY SCRIPTURE (BESIDE THE PSALTER)

IS APPOINTED TO BE READ.

THOLD Testament is appointed for the first lessons, at Morning and Evening prayer, and shall be read through, every year once, except certain books and Chapiters, which be least edifying, and might best bee spared, and therefore bee left unread.

The new Testament is appointed for the second Lessons, at Morning and Evening prayer, and shall be read over orderly every year thryse, beside the Epistles and Gospels: except the Apocalips [=Revelation], out of the which there bee only certain Lessons appointed, upon diverse proper feasts.

And to know what Lessons shall be read every day: find the day of the month in the Calendar following; and there ye shall perceive the books and Chapiters that shall be read for the Lessons, both at Morning and Evening prayer.

And here is to bee noted, that whenever there bee any proper Psalms or Lessons appointed for the Sondayes or for any feast moveable or unmovable: then the Psalms and Lessons, appointed in the calendar shall be omitted for that time.

Ye must note also that the Collect Epistle and Gospel, appointed for the Sunday shall serve al the weke after, except there fall some feast that hath his proper.

This is also to bee noted, concerning the Leap years, that the xxv day of February, which in Leap year is counted for two days, shall in those two days, alter nether Psalm nor Lesson: but the same Psalms and Lessons, which be said the first day, shall also serve for the second day.

Also, wheresoever the beginning of any Lesson, Epistle or Gospel is not expressed: there ye must begin at the beginning of the Chapiter.

And wheresoever is not expressed howe far shall be read, there shall you read to the end of the Chapiter.

* * *





A Brief Declaration

When Every Term Begins

and Ends

[After 1604, this is found at the very end of this section.]

BE it known that Easter Term begins always the eighteenth day after Easter, reckoning Easter Day for one. And ends the Monday next after Ascension Day.

Trinity Term begins always the Friday next after Trinity Sunday and ends the twenty-eighth day of June.

Michaelmas Term begins the ninth or tenth day of October and ends the twenty-eighth or twenty-ninth day of November.

Hilary Term begins the twenty-third or twenty-fourth day of January and ends the twelfth or thirteenth day of February.

In Easter Term on the Ascension Day, in Trinity Term on the Nativity of Saint John Baptist, in Michaelmas Term on the Feast of All Saints, in Hilary Term on the Feast of the Purification of our Lady, the Queen's judges of Westminster do not use to sit in judgment, nor upon any Sundays.

The following was added in 1561:



* * *



These to be observed for Holy days,

and none other.

THat is to say, All Sundays in the year. The days of the Feasts of the Circimcision of our Lord Jesus Chrsit. Of the Epiphany. Of the Purification of the blessed Virgin. Of S. Matthias the Apostle. Of the Enunciation of the blessed Virgin. Of S. Mark the Evangelist. Of S. Philip and Jacob Apostles. Of the Ascension of our Lord Jesus Christ. Of the Nativity of S. John Baptist. Of S. Peter the Apostle. Of S. James the Apostle. Of S. Bartholomew the Apostle. Of S. Matthew the Apostle. Of S. Michael the Archangel. Of S. Luke the Evangelist. Of S. Simon and Jude Apostles. Of All Saints. Of S. Andrew the Apostle. Of S. Thomas the Apostle. Of the Nativity of our Lord. Of S. Steven the Martyr. Of S. John Evangelist. Of the holy Innocents. Monday and Tuesday in Easter week. Monday and Tuesday in Whitsun week.

The Book of Common Prayer - 1559





Â¶ THE MINISTRACION OF BAPTISM

TO BE USED IN THE CHURCH.

It appears by ancient writers, that the Sacrament of Baptism in the old old time, was not commonly Ministered, but at two times in the year, at Easter and Whytsontide, at which times it was openly ministered in the presence of al the congregacion: which custom (now being grown out of use,) although it can not for many consideracions bee well restored again, yet it is thought good to follow the same as ne'er as conveniently may be. Wherefore the people are to be admonished, that it is most convenient that Baptism should not be ministered but upon Sondayes, and other holy days, when the most nombre of people may come together, as well for that the congregacion there present may testify the receiving of them that be newly Baptised into the number of Christ's Church, as also because in the Baptism of Infants every man present may be put in remembrance of his awne profession made to God in his Baptism. For which cause also, it is expedient that Baptism be ministered in the English tongue. Nevertheless (if necessity so require) children may at al times be Baptised at home.

Â¶	When there are children to he baptised upon the Sunday, or holy day, the parents shall geve knowledge over night, or in the morning, before the beginning of Morning prayour, to the curate. A nd then the Godfathers, Godmothers, and people with the children, must be ready at the Font, either immediately after the last Lesson at Morning Prayour, or else immediately after the last Lesson at Evening Praiour, as the Curate by his discretion shall appoincte. And then standing there, the Priest shall ask whether the children be Baptised or no. If they answer, No. Then the priest say thus.

DEARLY beloved, forasmuch as al men be conceived and borne in sin, and that our saviour Christ saith, none can entry into the kingdom of God (except he be regenerate, and borne a new of water and the holy gost) I beseech you to cal upon God the father, through our lord Jesus Christ, that of his bounteous mercy, he will grant to these children, that thing which by nature they can not have, that they may be baptised with water and the holy Ghost, and received into Christ's holy church; and be made lively members of the same.

Then the Priest shall say.

Let us pray.

ALMIGHTY and everlasting God, which of thy great mercy did save No and his family in the Arcke, from perishing by water, and also did safely lead the children of Israel, thy people, through the red Sea, figuring thereby thy holy Baptism: and by the Baptism of thy well-beloved son Jesus Christ, did sanctify the floude Jordan, and al other waters, to the mistical washinge away of sin: We beseech the (for thine infinite mercies) that thou wilt mercifully loke upon these children, sanctify them and wash them with thy* holy gost, that they being delivered from thy wrath, may be received into the Arcke of Christ's church, and being steadfast in faith, joyful through hope, and roted in charity, may so pass the waves of this troublesome world, that finally they may come to the land of everlasting life, there to reign with the, world without end, through Jesus Christ our Lord. Amen.



* "the" in 1604.





ALMIGHTY and immortal God, the aide of al that need, the helper of al that fly to the for succour, the life of them that believe, and the resurrection of the dead, we cal upon the for these infants, that they, coming to thy holy Baptism, may receive remission of their sins by spiritual regeneracion, receive them (O Lord) as thou haste promised by thy well-beloved son, saying: Ask and you shall have; seek, and you shall find: knock and it shall be opened unto you: So geve now unto us that ask. Let us that seek, find open thy gate unto us that knock, that these infants enjoy the everlasting benediction of thy heavenly washing, and may come to the eternal kingdom which thou haste promised by Christ our Lord. Amen.

Â¶ Then shall the Priest say

Hear the words of the Gospel, written by Saint Mark in the tenth Chapiter.





AT a certain time they brought children to Christ that he should touche them, and his Disciples rebuked those that brought them. But when Jesus saw it, he was displeased, and said unto them. Suifre little children to come unto me, and forbid them not; For to such belongs the Kingdom of God. Verily, I say unto you; whosoever doth not receive the kingdom of God, as a little child: he shall not entry therein. And when he had taken the up in his arms: he put his hands upon them, and blessed them.

Â¶ After the Gospel is red, the minister shall make this brief exhortacion upon the words of the Gospel.

FRIENDS, ye hear in this Gospel the words of our saviour Christ, that he commanded the children to bee brought unto him: howe he blamed those that would have kept them from him, how he exhorted all men to follow their innocence. Ye perceive how by his outward gesture and dede he declared his good will toward them. For he embraced them in his arms, he laid his hands upon them, and blessed them, doubt not you therefore, but earnestly believe that he will likewise favourably receive these present infants, that he will embrace the with the arms of his mercy, that he will geve unto them the blessing of eternal life: and make them partakers of his everlasting kingdom. Wherefore we being thus persuaded of the good will of our heavenly father, towards these infants declared by his son Jesus Christ, and nothing doubting, but that he favourably allows this charitable work of ours, in bringing these children to his holy Baptism: let us faithfully and devoutly geve thakes unto him, and say

ALMIGHTY and everlasting God, heavenly Father, we geve thee humble thanks, that thou haste vouchedsaufe to call us to the knowledge of thy grace and faith in the, increase this knowledge, and confirm this faith in us evermore: Geve thy holy spirit to these infants, that they may be borne again, and be made heirs of everlasting salvation, through our Lord Jesus Christ. who lives and reigns with the, and the holy spirit, now and for ever. Amen.

Then the Priest shall speak unto the Godfathers and Godmothers, on this wise:

WELL-BELOVED friends, ye have brought these children here to be baptised, ye have prayed that our lord Jesus christ, would vouchesaufe to receive them, to lay his hands upon them, to bless them, to release them of their sins, to geve them the kingdom of heaven, and everlasting life. Ye have heard also that our Lord Jesus Christ hath promised in his Gospel, to grant all these things that ye have prayed for: which promise he for his part will most surely keep and perform. Wherefore after this promise made by Christ, these infants must also faithfully for their part promise by you that be their sureties, that they will forsake the devil and al his works, and constantly believe Gods holy word, and obediently keep his commandments.

Then shall the Priest demand of the Godfathers and Godmothers these questions.

DOEST thou forsake the devil and all his works, the vain pomp and glory of the world, with al covetous desires of the same, and the carnal desires of the flesh, so that thou wilt not follow, nor be led by them?

Answer. I forsake them al.

The Minister. Doest thou believe in god the father almighty, maker of heave and earth? And in Jesus christ his only begotten son our Lord, and that he was conceived by the holy Ghost, borne of the virgin Mary: that he suifred under Poncius Pilot, was crucified, dead and buried, that he went down into hell, and also did rise again the third day: that he ascended into heaven, and sits at the right had of god the father almighty; and from thence shall come again at the end of the world, to judge the quick and the dead? And doest thou believe in the holy Ghost the holy Catholicque Church, the communion of saints, the remission of sins, the resurreccion of the flesh, and everlasting life after death?

Answer. All this I steadfastly believe.

Ministry. Will thou be baptised in this faith?

Answer. That is my desire.



Mark x.

Â¶ Then shall the Priest say.

O MERCIFUL God, grant that the old Adam in these children may be so buried, that the new man may be raised up in them. Amen.

Grant that all carnal affeccions may dye in them, and that all things belonging to the spirit may live and grow in them. Amen.

Grant that they may have power and strength to have victory, and to triumph against the Devil, the world, and the flesh. Amen.

Grant that whosoever is here dedicated to thee, by our office and ministry, may also be endued with heavenly virtues, and everlastingly rewarded through thy mercy, O blessed Lord God, who doest live and govern al things world without end. Amen.

ALMIGHTY everliving God, whose most dearly beloved son Jesus Christ, for the forgiveness of our sins, did shed out his most precious side both water and blood, and gave commandment to his disciples that they should go teach al nations, and baptise them in the name of the father, the son, and of the holy Ghost : Regard, we beseech the, the supplicacions of thy congregacion, and grant that al thy servants which shall be baptised in this water, may receive the fulness of thy grace, and ever remain in the nombre of thy faithful and elect children, through Jesus Christ our Lord. Amen.

Then the Priest shall take the Child in his hands, and ask the name; and naming the Child, shall dip it in the water, so it be discreetly and warily done, saying,

N. I Baptise the in the name of the Father, and of the Son, and of the holy Ghost. Amen.

Â¶ And if the Ghilde be weak, it shall suffice to power water upon it, saying the foresaid words.

N. I Baptise the in the name of the Father, and of the son, and of the holy Ghost. Amen.

Then the Priest shall make a Cross upon the Childes forehead, saying:

WE receive this Child into the congregacion of Christ's flock, and do sign him with the sign of the cross, in token that hereafter he shall not be ashamed to confess the faith of Christ crucified, and manfully to fight under his banner against sin, the world, and the devil, and to continue Christ's faithful soldier and servant unto his lives end. Amen.

Then shall the Priest say,

SAYING now, dearly beloved brethren that these children be regenerate and graffed [grafted] into the body of Christ's congregacion, let us geve thanks unto God for these benefits, and with one accord make our praiours unto almighty God, that they may lead the rest of their life according to this beginning.

Then shall be said.

Our Father which art &c.

Then shall the Priest say,

We yield the hearty thanks most merciful father, that it has pleased thee to regenerate this infant with thy holy spirit, to receive him for thine own child by adoption, and to incorporate him into thy holy congregacion. And humbly we beseech thee to grant that he being dead unto sin and living unto righteousness, and being buried with Christ in his death, may crucify the old man, and utterly abolish the whole body of sin, that as he is made partaker of the death of thy son, so he may be partaker of his resurreccion, so that finally with the residue of thy holy congregacion, he may be inheritor of thine everlasting kingdom. Through Christ our Lord. Amen.

Â¶ At the last end, the Priest calling the Godfathers and Godmothers together, shall say this short exhortation following.

FORASMUCH as these children have promised by you to forsake the Devil and his works, to believe in God, and to serve him, you must remember that it is your parts and duties to see that these infants be taught, so soon as they shall be able to learn, what a solemn vow, promise, and profession they have made by you. And that they may know these things the better; ye shall cal upon them to hear Sermons, And chiefly you shall provide that they may learn the Cred, the Lords prayer, and the Ten Commandments in the English tongue; and al other things which a Christian man ought to know and believe to his souls health. And that these children may be virtuously brought up, to lead a Godly and a christian life, remembering always that Baptism doth represent unto us our profession, which is to follow the example of our saviour Christ, and to be made like unto him, that as he died and rose again for us: so should we (which are Baptised) dye from sin, and rise again unto rightuousnes, continually mortifiyng al our evil and corrupt affections, and daily proceeding in all virtue and godliness of living.

Â¶	The Minister shall command that the children be brought to the Bishop to be confirmed of him, so soon as they can say in their vulgar tongue the articles of the faith, the Lords prayer, and the x. Commandments, and be further instructed in the Catechism set furs for that purpose, accordingly as it is there expressed.





OF THEM THAT BE

BAPTISED IN PRIVATE HOUSES,

IN TIME OF NECESSITY.

[BY THE LAWFUL MINISTER OF THE PARISH, OR ANY OTHER LAWFUL MINISTER, THAT CAN BE PROCURED.]*



* Added in 1604.





Â¶	The Pastors and Curates shall oft admonish the people, that they defer not the Baptism of infants any longer then the Sunday, or other holy day, next after the child be borne unless upon a great and reasonable cause declared to the Curate, and by him approved.



1559:

And also they shall warn them that without great cause, and necessity, they baptise not children at home in their houses. And when great need shall compelle them so to doe, that then they minister on this fassion.

First let them that be present cal upon God for his grace, and say the Lords prayour, if the time will sufre. And then one of them shall name the child, and dip him in the water, or power water upon him, saying these words.

1604:

And also they shall warn them, that without great cause and necessity, they procure not their children to be baptised at home in their houses. And when great need shall compel them so to do, that then Baptism shall be administered in this fashion.

First, let the lawful Minister, and them that be present, call upon God for his grace and say the Lord's Prayer, if the time will suffer. And then the child being named by some one that is present, the said lawful Minister shall dip it in water, or pour water upon it, saying these words.





N. I Baptise the in the name of the Father, and of the Son, and of the holy Ghost. Amen.

And let them not doubt, but that the child so Baptised, is lawfully and sufficiently Baptised, and ought not to be Baptised again in the Church. But yet nevertheless, if the child which is after this sort Baptised, do afterward live, it is expediente that he be brought into the Church, to the intent the Priest may examine and try, whether the child be lawfully Baptised or no. And if those that bring any child to the Church do answer that he is already Baptised: then shall the Priest examine them further.





N. I Baptise thee in the Name of the Father, and of the Son, and of the holy Ghost. Amen.

And let them not doubt, but that the child so Baptised, is lawfully and sufficiently Baptised, and ought not to be Baptised again in the Church. But yet nevertheless, if the child which is after this sort Baptised, do afterward live, it is expediente that he be brought into the Church, to the intent that if the Priest or Minister of the same Parish did himself baptise that child, the Congregation may be certified of the true form of Baptism, by him privately before used: Or if the child were baptised by any other lawful Minister, that then the Minister of the Parish where the child was borne or Christened, shall examine and try whether this child be lawfully baptised, or no. In which case, if those that bring any child to the Church, do answer that the same child is already baptised, then shall the Minister examine them further, saying,





Â¶ By whom the child was Baptised?

Â¶ Who was present when the child was Baptised?

Â¶ Whether they called upon God for grace and succour in that necessity?

Â¶ With what thing, or what matter they did Baptise the Child?

Â¶ With what words the child was Baptised?

Â¶ Whether they think the child to be lawfully and perfectly Baptised?

Â¶ By whom the child was baptised?

Â¶ Who was present when the child was baptised?

Â¶ And because some things essential to this Sacrament may happen to be omitted through fear or haste in such times of extremity; therefore I demand further of you,

Â¶ With what matter was the child baptised?

Â¶ With what words was the child baptised?

Â¶ Whether think you the child to bee lawfully and perfectly baptised?





Â¶	And if the Minister shall prove* by the answers of such, as brought* the child, that all things were done as they ought to be: Then shall not he Christen the child again, but shall receive him, as one of the flock of the true Christian people, saiynge thus.

I CERTIFY you, that in this case ye have done well*, and according unto due ordre concerning the Baptising of this child, which being borne in Original sin and in the wrath of God, is now by the laver [=water] of regeneracion in Baptism, received into the number of the children of God, and heirs of everlasting life, for our Lord Jesus Christ doth not deny his grace and mercy unto such infants, but most lovingly doth cal the unto him: as the holy gospel doth witness to our comfort on this wise.



* "find" and "bring" in 1604.



* "all is well done" in 1604.



AT a certain time they brought children unto Christ that he should touche them, and his disciples rebuked those that brought them. But when Jesus saw it, he was displeased, and said unto them: Suffer little children to come unto me, and forbid them not, for to such belongs the kingdom of God. Verily I say unto you, whosoever doth not receive the kingdom of God as a little child, he shall not entry therein. And when he had taken them up in his arms, he put his hands upon them, and blessed them.

Â¶ After the Gospel is red, the minister shall make this exhortacion upon the words of the Gospel.

FRIENDS, ye hear in this Gospel the words of our saviour Christ, that he commanded the children to bee brought unto him: howe he blamed those that would have kept them from him, howe he exhorted all men to follow their innocence: Ye perceive how by his outward gesture in dede he declared his good will toward them. For he embraced them in his arms, he laid his hands upon them, and blessed them, doubt not you therefore, but earnestly believe, that he hath likewise favourably received this present infant, that he has embraced him with the arms of his mercy, that he hath given unto him the blessing of eternal life, and made him partaker of his everlasting kingdom. Wherefore we being thus persuaded of the good will of our heavenly father declared by his son Jesus Christ towards this infant, Let us faithfully and devoutly geve thanks unto him, and say the prayer, which the lord him self taught, and in declaration of our faith, let us recite the articles contained in our Cred.

Â¶ Here the Minister with the Godfathers, and Godmothers shall say.

OUR Father which &c.

Â¶	Then the Priest shall demand the name of the child, which being by the Godfathers, and Godmothers pronounced, the Minister shall say,

Â¶ DOEST thou in the name of this child forsfake the devil, and al his works, the vain pomp, and glory of the world, with al the covetous desires of the same, the carnal desires of the flesh, and not to follow and be led by them?

Answer. I forsake them al.

Â¶ The Minister. Doest thou in the name of this child profess this faith, to believe in God the father almighty, maker of heaven and earth And in Jesus Christ his only begotten son our Lord, and that he was conceived by the holy ghost, borne of the virgin Mary: that he suffered under ponce Pilot, was crucified, dead, and buried, that he wet down into hell, and also did rise again the iii day: that he ascended into heaven, and sits at the right hand of God the father almighty: and from thence he shall come again at the end of the world, to judge the quick and the dead? And do you in his name believe in the holy gost the holy Catholicque church, the communion of saints, the remission of sins, resurreccion of the flesh, and everlasting life after death?

Answer. All this I steadfastly believe.

Let us pray.

ALMIGHTY and everlasting God, heavenly father, we geve thee humble thanks, for that thou hast vouchedsafed to call us to the knowledge of thy grace and faith in thee: increase this knowledge, and confirm this faith in us evermore: Geve thy holy spirit to this infant,that he being borne again and being made heir of everlasting salvation, through our Lord Jesus Christ, may continue thy servant, and attain thy promise, through the same our Lord Jesus Christ thy son, who lives and reigns with the in the unity of the same holy spirit everlasting. Amen.

Then shall the Minister make this exhortacion, to the Godfathers and Godmothers.

FORASMUCH as this child hath promised by you to forsake the devil and al his works, to believe in God, and to serve him: you must remember that it is your part and duty, to see that this infant be taught (so soon as he shall be able to learn) what a solemn vow promise, and profession he hath made by you. And that he may know these things the better, ye shall call upon him to hear sermons. And chiefly ye shall provide that he may learn the Cred, the Lords prayer and the x Commandments in the English tongue, and al other things which a Christian man ought to know, and believe to his souls health, and that this child may be virtuously brought up, to lead a godly, and a christian life. Remembering always that Baptism doth represent unto us our profession, which is to follow the example of our Saviour Christ, and be made like unto him, that as he died and rose again for us, so should we which are Baptised, dye from sin, and rise again unto righteousness, continually mortifying all our evil and corrupt affections, and daily proceeding in al virtue, and godliness of living, etc:

Â¶ As in Public Baptism.

Â¶	But if they which bring the infants to the Church, do make an uncertain answer* to the Priests questions, and say that they cannot tel what they thought, did, or said, in yt great fear, and trouble of mind: (as oft times it chaunseth) then let the Priest Baptise him in form above written, concerning public Baptism, saving that at the dipping of the child in the Font, he shall use this form af words.

If thou be not Baptised al ready, N. I baptise the in the name of the father, and of the Son, and of the holy Ghost. Amen.

Mark x.

* "such uncertain answers" in 1604.

THE ORDER FOR THE

BURIAL OF THE DEAD.

Â¶	The priest meting the corpse at the Church style, shall say, Or else the priests and clerks shall sing, and so go either unto* the church, or towards the grave.



* "into" in 1604.



	I AM the resurrection and the life (saith the Lord) he that beleveth in me: yea, though he were dead, yet shall he live. And whosoever lives, and believes in me, shall not dye for ever.





Jhon xi.

I KNOW that my redemer lyveth, and that I shall rise out of the earth in the last day, and shall be covered again with my skin, and shall se God in my flesh: yea, and I my self shall behold him, not with other, but with the same eyes.





Job xix.

	WE brought nothing into this world, neither may we cary any thing out of this world.



i. Tim. vi.

	 The Lord gives, and the Lord takes away. Even as it hath pleased the Lord so comes things to pass: Blessed be the name of the Lord.

Â¶	When they come to the grave, while the corps is made ready to be laid into the earth, ye priest shall say, or the priests, and clerks shall sing.



Job i.

	MAN that is borne of a woman has but a short time to lyve, and is full of misery: he comes up, and is cut down like a flower, he flies as it were a shadow, and never continues in one staye. In the midst of life we be in death, of whom my we seek for succour but of the, O Lord, which for our sins justly art displeased: yet O Lord God most holy, O Lord most mighty, O holy, and most merciful Saviour, deliver us not into the bitter pains of eternal death. Thou know Lord the secretes of our hertes, shut not up thy merciful eyes to our prayers. But spare us Lord most holy, O God most mighty, O holy and merciful Saviour, thou most worthy judge eternal, suffer us not at our last hour for any pains of death to fall from the.

Â¶ Then while the earth shall be cast upon the body by some standing by, the priest shall say.

FOR as much as it hath pleased almighty God of his great mercy to take unto him self the Soul of our dear brother, here departed, we therefore commit his body to the ground, earth, to earth ashes, to ashes, dust, to dust, in sure, and certain hope of resurrection to eternal life, through our Lord Jesus Christ, who shall change our vile body that it may be like to his glorious body, according to the mighty working whereby he is able to subdue al things to him self.

Then shall be said, or songe.

I HEARD a voice from heaven saying unto me, write from hencefurth, blessed are the dead which dye in the Lord. Even so says the spirit that they rest from their labours.



Job xi.

Then shall follow this lesson, taken out of the . xv. Chap. to the Corin. the first Epistle.

CHRIST is risen from the dead, and become the first fruit of them that slept. For by a man came death, and by a man came the resurreccion of the dead. For as by Adam al die, even so by Christ shall al be made alive, but every manne in his own order. The first is Christ, then they that are Christ's at his coming. Then comes the end when he has delivered up the kyngedome to God the father, when he hath put down all rule, and all authority and power. For he must reign till he have put his enemies under his fete. The last enemy that shall be destroyed is death. For he hath put all things under his feet. But when he says, all things are put under him, it is manifest that hee is excepted, which did put all things under him. When al things are subdued unto him, then shall the son also him self be subject unto him that put all things under him, that God may be al in all, else what do they which are baptised over the dead, if the dead rise not at all? Why are they then baptised over them: yea, and why stand we always then in jeopardy? By our rejoicing which I have in Christ jesu our Lord, I dye daily. That I have fought with beasts Ephesus after the manner of men, what avauntageth it me, if the dead rise not again? Let us eat and drink, for to morrow we shall dye. Be not ye deceived; evil words corrupt good manners. Awake truly out of sleep, and sin not. For sum have not the knowledge of God. I speak this to your shame. But some manne will say how arise the dead? with what body shall they come? thou fool, that which thou sowest is not quickened except it dye. And what sowest thou? thou sowest not that body that shall be; but bare corn [=seed], as of wheat, or some other: but God gives it a body at his pleasure, to every sede his own body. All flesh is not one manner of flesh: but there is one manner of flesh of men, an other manner of flesh of beasts, an other of fishes, an other of birds. There are also celestial bodies, and there are bodies terrestrial. But the glory of the celestial is one, and the glory of the terrestrial is another. There is one manner glory of the Son, and another glory of the Moan [Moon], and another glory of the stars. For one star differs from another in glory: so is the resurrection of the dead. It is sown in corrupcion, it rises again in incorrupcion. It is sown in dishonour, it rises again in honour. It is sown in weakness, it rises again in power. It is sown a natural body, it rises again a spiritual body. There is a natural body, and there is a spiritual body: as it is also written, the first man Adam was made a living soul, and the last Adam was made a quickening spirit. How be it that is not first which is spiritual: but that which is natural and then that which is spiritual. The first man is of the earth, earthy : The second manne is the Lord from Heaven (heavenly). As is the earthy, such are they that be earthy. And as is the heavenly, such are they that are heavenly. And as we have borne the image of the earthy, so shall we bear the image of the heavenly. This say I brethren, that flesh and blood cannot inherit the kingdom of God, neither doth corruption inherit incorruption. Behold, I show you a mystery. we shall not all sleep: but we shall al be changed, and that in a moment, in the twynkelynge of an eye by the last trump [trumpet]. For the trump shall blow, and the dead shall rise incorruptible, and we shall be changed. For this corruptible must put on incorruption, and this mortal must put on immortality. When this corruptible hath put on incorruption, and this mortal hath put on immortality: then shall be brought to pass the saying that is written, Death is swallowed up in victory: Death, where is thy sting? Hell where is thy victory? The sting of death is sin, and the strength of sin is the law. But thanks be unto God, which has given us victory, through our Lord Jesus Christ. Therefore my dear brethren, be ye steadfast and unmovable, always rich in the work of the lord, forasmuch as ye know, howe that your labour is not in vain in the Lord.

Â¶ The Lesson ended, the Priest shall say.

Lord have mercy upon us.

Christ have mercy upon us.

Lord have mercy upon us.

Our Father which art in heaven. &c.

And lead us not into temptation.

Answer. But deliver us from evil. Amen.



Â¶ The Priest.

ALMIGHTY God, with whom do live the spirits of them that depart hence in the lord and in whom the souls of them that be elected, after they be delivered from the burden of the flesh, be in joy and felicity. We geve the hearty thanks for that it hath pleased the to deliver this N. our brother, out of the miseries of this synneful world beseeching the that it may please the of thy gracious goodness, shortly to accomplish the number of thine elect, and to haste thy kyngedome, that we with this our brother, and all other departed in the true faith of thy holy name, may have our perfect consummacion and bliss, both in body and soul in thy eternal and everlasting glory. Amen.

Â¶ The Collect.

O MERCIFUL God, the father of our Lord Jesus Christ, who is the Resurrection and the life, in whom whosoever beleveth shall live, though he dye, and whosoever lives, and beleveth in him, shall not dye eternally, who also taught us (by his holy apostle Paule), not to be sorry as men without hope, for them that sleep in him: We mekely beseech the (O Father) to raise us from the death of sin unto the life of righteousness, that when we shall depart this life, we may rest in him, as our hope is this our brother doth, and that at the general resurrection in the last day, we may be found acceptable in thy sight, and receive that blessing which thy well-beloved son shall then pronounce to all that love and fear the, saiynge: Come ye blessed children of my father, receive the Kyngedome prepared for you from the beginning of the world. Grant this, we beseech the, O merciful father, through Jesus Christ our mediator and redemer. Amen.

Â¶ THE THANKESGEVINGE OF WOMEN

AFTER CHILD BIRTH,

COMMUNELYE CALLED

THE CHURCHYNGE OF WOMEN.



The woman shall come into the church, and there shall kneel down in some convenient place, nigh unto the place where the table stands, and the priest standing by her, shall say these words, or such like, as the case that require.

FORASMUCH as it hath pleased almighty God of his goodness to geve you safe deliverance, and hath preserved you in the great danger of childbirth: ye shall therefore geve hearty thanks unto God and pray.

Â¶ Then shall the priest say this Psalm.

I HAVE lift up mine eyes unto the hills, from whence comes my help.

My help comes even from the Lord: which hath made heaven and earth.

He will not suifre thy foot to be moved: and he that kepeth the, will not sleep.

Behold, he that kepeth Israel: shall neither slumber nor sleep.

The Lord him self is thy keeper: the Lord is thy defence upon thy right hand.

So that the son shall not burn the by day, neither the moon by night.

The Lord shall preserve the from al evil: yea, it is even he that shall keep thy soul.

The Lord shall preserve thy going out, and thy coming in: from this time forth for evermore.

Glory be to the Father, and to the Son &c.

As it was in the beginning, is now &c.

Lord have mercy upon us.

Christ have mercy upon us.

Lord have mercy upon us.

OUR FATHER WHICH ART &c.

And lead us not into temptation.

Answer. But deliver us from evil. Amen.

Priest.* O Lord save this woman thy servant.

Answer. Which puts her trust in the.

Priest.* Be thou to her a strong Tower.

Answer. From the face of her enemy.

Priest.* Lord hear our prayer.

Answer. And let our cry come unto the.

Priest.*

* "Minister" in 1604.



Let us pray.

O ALMIGHTY God, which hast delivered this woman thy servant from the great pain and peril of child birth: Grant we beseech the most merciful Father, that she through thy help may both faithfully live, and walk in her vocation, according to thy will, in this life present, and also may be partaker of everlasting glory in the life to come, through Jesus Christ our Lord. Amen.

The woman that comes to gin her thanks, must offer accustomed offerings, and if there be a Communion, it is convenient that she receive the holy Communion.



* * *





A COMMINATION AGAINST SINNERS,

WITH CERTAIN PRAYERS, TO BE USED DIVERS TIMES IN THE YEAR.



After Morning prayer, the people being called together by the ringing of a Bell, and assembled in the Church, thenglish Litany shall be said after thaccustomed manner, which ended the priest shall go into the pulpit and say thus.

BRETHREN, in the Primitive church there was a godly discipline, that at the beginning of Lent, such persons as were notoryus Sinners, were put to open penance and punished in this world, that their souls might be saved in the day of the lord. And that others admonished by their example might be more afraid to offend. In the stead whereof (until the said Discipline may be restored again, which thing is much to be wished) it is thought good that at this time (in your presence) should be red the general sentences of gods cursing against impenitent Sinners, gathered out of the .xxvii. Chapiter of Deuteronomye, and other places of Scripture. And that ye should answer to every sentence. Amen. To the intent that you being admonished of the great indignation of God against Sinners: may the rather be called to earnest and true repentance, and may walk more warily in these dangerous days, fleeing from such vices, for the which ye affirm with your own mouths, the Curse of God to be due.

CURSED is the man that makes any carved, or molten Image, an abomination to the Lord, the work of the hands of the crafts man, and puts it in a secrete place to worship it.

Â¶ And the people shall answer and say

Amen.

Minister. Cursed is he that cursethe his father, or mother.

Answer. Amen.

Minister. Cursed is hee that removes away the marcke of his neighbours land.

Answer. Amen.

Minister. Cursed is he that makes the blind to go out of his way.

Answer. Amen.

Minister. Cursed is he that, lets [=hinders] in judgmet, the right of the stranger, of them that be fatherless, and of widows.

Answer. Amen.

Minister. Cursed is he that smites his neighbour secretly.

Answer. Amen.

Minister. Cursed is he that lies with his neighbours wife.

Answer. Amen.

Minister. Cursed is he that takes reward to slay the Soul of innocent blood.

Answer. Amen.

Minister. Curses is he that puts his trust in manne, and takes manne for his defence, and in his heart goes from the Lord.

Answer. Amen.

Minister. Cursed are the unmerciful, the fornicatours, and adulterers, and the covetous persons, the worshippers of images, slanderers, dronkardes, and extorcioners.

Answer. Amen.

The Minister.





Now saying that all they be accursed (as the Prophet David bears witness) [Psa. cxviii. =Ps. 119:21] which do err, and go astray from the cornmaundernentes of God, let us remembering the dreadful judgement hanging over our heads, and being always at hand return unto our Lord God, with all contricion and mekenes of heart, bewailing and lamenting our sinful life, knowledging [=acknowledging] and confessing our offences, and seeking to bring furs worthy fruits of penance. For now is the Axe put unto the root of the trees, so that every tree which brings not furs good fruit, is hewn down and cast into the fire. [Math. iii.] It is a fearful thing to fall into the hands of the living God: [Heb. x.] he shall pour down rain upon the sinners, Snares, fire, and brimstone, storm and tempest, this shall be their portion to drink.[Psal. x. = Ps. 11:6] For lo, the Lord is common out of his place, to visit the wickedness of such as dwell upon the earth. [Esai. (Isaiah) xxvi.] But who may abide the day of his coming? Who shall be able to endure, when he apereth? [Mal. iii.] His fan is in his hand, and he will pourge his floor, and gather his wheat into the barn, but he will burn the chafe with unquenchable fire. [Math. iii.] The day of the Lord comes as a thief upon the night, and when men shall say peace, and all things are sauf, then shall soubdenly destruction come upon them, as sorrow comes upon a woman travailing with child, and they shall not escape. [i. Thes. v.] Then shall appear the wrath of God in the day of vengeance, which obstinate sinners, through the stubburnnes of their heart, have heaped unto them self, [Rom. ii.] which despised the goodness, patience, and lunge sufferance of God, when he called them continually to repentance. Then shall they call upon me, says the Lord, but I will not hear: they shall seek me early, but they shall not find me: and that because they hated knowledge, and received not the fear of the Lord, but abhorred my counsel, and despised my correcyon, [Prover. i.] then shall it be to late to knock, when the door shall be shut, and to late to cry for mercy, when it is the tyrne of Justice. O terrible voice of most just judgement, which shall be 	pronounced upon them, when it shall be said unto them: Go, ye cursed, into the fire everlasting, which is prepared for the devil 	and his Aungeles. [Mat. xxv.] Therefore brethren take we heed by time, [betime, =in good time] while the day of salvation lasts, [ii. Cor. vi.] for the night comes when none can 	work: [Jhon ix.] but let us while we have the light, believe in the light, and walk as the children of the light, that we be not caste into the 	utter darckenes, where is wepyinge and gnasshynge of teeth. [Mat. xxv.] Let us not abuse the goodness of God, which calls us mercifully to amendment, and of his endelesse pytye promised us forgiveness of that which is paste [past]: If (with a whole mind and true heart) 	we return unto him. For though our sins be red as scarlet, they shall be as white as snow, and though they be like purple, 	yet shall they be as white as wolle. [Esay. (Isaiah) i.] Turn you clean (says the Lord) from all your wickedness, and your sin shall not be your destruction. [Ezechiel xxviii. =Ezek. 18] Cast away from you all your ungodliness that ye have done: make you new hearts, and a new spirit: wherefore will ye dye, O ye house of Israel? Seiyng that I have no pleasure in the death of him that dies (says the Lord God.) Turn you then, and you shall lyve. Although we have synned, yet have we an advocate with the Father, Jesus Christ the righteous, and he it 	is that obteyneth grace for our sins, [i. Jhon ii.] for he was wounded for our offences, and smitten for our wickedness. [Esai. liii.] Let us therefore return unto him, who is the merciful receiver of all true penitent sinners, assuring our self that he is ready to receive us, and most willing to pardon us, if we come to him, with faithful repentance. If we will submit our selves unto him, and from hencefurthe walk in his ways. If we will take his easy yoke, and light burden upon us, [Math. xi.] to follow him in lowliness, patience, and charity, and be ordered by the governance of his holy spirit, seking always his glory, and serving him duly in our vocation with thanks gevynge. This if we do, Christ will deliver us from the curse of the law, and from the extreme malediction, which light upon them, that shall be set 	on the left hand, and he will set us on his right hand, and geve us the blessed benediction of his father, commanding us to take possession of his glorious kingdom, [Math. xxv.] unto the which he vouchesaufe to bring us al, for his infinite mercy.

Â¶	Then shall they all kneel upon their knees: And the Priests and Clerckes knelynge (were they are accustomed to say the Litany) shall say thy: Psalm. Miserere mei Deus.





The scripture references seen here within the text were placed in the margin in the original.



HAVE mercy upon me, O God after thy great goodness, according to the multitude of thy mercies, do away mine offences,

Wash me thoroughly from my wickedness and cleanse me from my sin.

For I acknowledge my faults, and my sin is ever before me.

Against the only have I synned, and done this evil in thy sight, that thou might be justified in thy saying, and clear when thou art judged.

Behold, I was shapen in wickedness, and in sin hath my mother conceived me.

But lo, thou require truth in inward parties [parts], and shalt make me to understand wisdom secretly.

Thou shalt purge me with hysoppe, and I shall be clean, thou shalt wash me, and I shall be whyter then Snow.

Thou shalt make me here of joy and gladness : that the bones which thou hast broken may rejoice.

Turn thy face from my sins: and put out all my misdedes.

Make me a clean heart (O God:) and renew a right spirit within me.

Cast me not away from thy presence : and take not thy holy spirit from me.

O geve me the comfort of thy help again: and stablysh me with thy free spirit.

Then shall I teach thy ways unto the wicked : and sinners shall be converted unto the.

Deliver me from blood giltines (O God) thou that art the God of my health: and my tongue shall singe of thy righteousness.

Thou shalt open my lips (O Lord) my mouth shall show thy praise.

For thou desire no sacrifice, else would I geve it the: but thou delight not in burnt offering.

The sacrifice of God is a troubled spirit: a broken and a contrite heart O God, shalt thou not despise.

O be favourable and gracious unto Zion : build thou the walls of Jerusalem.

Then shalt thou be pleased with the sacrifice of rightuousnesse, with the burnt offerings and oblations : then shall they offer young bullocks upon thine aultare.

Glory bee to the Father, and to the Son, and to the holy Ghost.

As it was in the beginning, is now, and ever shall be world without end. Amen.

Lord have mercy upon us.

Christ have mercy upon us.

Lord have mercy upon us.

Our father which art in heaven. &c.

And lead us not into temptation.

Answer. But deliver us from evil. Amen.

Minister. O Lord save thy servauntes.

Answer. Which put their trust in the.

Minis/er. Send unto them help from above.

Answer. And evermore mightily defend them.

Minister. Help us, O God our saviour.

Answer. And for the glory of thy names sake deliver us, bee merciful unto us sinners, for thy names sake.

The Minister. Lord hear my prayers.

Answer. And let our cry come unto thee.

Let us pray.

O LORD, we beseech the, mercifully hear our prayers, and spare al those which confess their sins to the, that they (whose consciences by sin are accused) by thy merciful pardon may be absolved, through Christ our Lord. Amen.

O MOST mighty God, and merciful father which haste compassion of al men, and hate nothing that thou haste made: which would not the death of a sinner, but that he should rather turn from sin, and be saved: mercifully forgeve us our trespasses, and comfort us, which be grieved and wearied [wearied] with the burden of our sin. Thy property is to have mercy, to the only it appertains to forgeve sins: spare us therefore good Lord, spare thy people whom thou haste redeemed. Enter not into judgement with thy servauntes, which be vile earth, and miserable sinners, but so turn thine ire [ire] from us which mekely knowledge [=acknowledge] our vileness, and truly repent us of our faults: so make haste to help us in this world, that we may ever live with thee in the world to come, through Jesus Christ our Lord. Amen.

Then shall the people say this that follows after the Minister.

TURN thou us, O good Lord, and so shall we be turned: be favourable O Lord bee favourable too thy people, which turn to the, in weeping, fasting, and praying, for thou art a merciful God, full of compassion, lunge suffering, and of a great pity. Thou sparest when we deserve punishment, and in thy wrath think upon mercy, spare thy people good Lord, spare them, and let not thy heritage be brought to confusion: hear us O Lord for thy mercy is great, and after the multitude of thy mercies, loke upon us.



Psal. li.

The sacrifice of God is a troubled spirit: a broken and a contrite heart O God, shalt thou not despise.

O be favourable and gracious unto Zion : build thou the walls of Jerusalem.

Then shalt thou be pleased with the sacrifice of rightuousnesse, with the burnt offerings and oblations : then shall they offer young bullocks upon thine aultare.

Glory bee to the Father, and to the Son, and to the holy Ghost.

As it was in the beginning, is now, and ever shall be world without end. Amen.

Lord have mercy upon us.

Christ have mercy upon us.

Lord have mercy upon us.

Our father which art in heaven. &c.

And lead us not into temptation.

Answer. But deliver us from evil. Amen.

Minister. O Lord save thy servauntes.

Answer. Which put their trust in the.

Minis/er. Send unto them help from above.

Answer. And evermore mightily defend them.

Minister. Help us, O God our saviour.

Answer. And for the glory of thy names sake deliver us, bee merciful unto us sinners, for thy names sake.

The Minister. Lord hear my prayers.

Answer. And let our cry come unto thee.

Let us pray.

O LORD, we beseech the, mercifully hear our prayers, and spare al those which confess their sins to the, that they (whose consciences by sin are accused) by thy merciful pardon may be absolved, through Christ our Lord. Amen.

O MOST mighty God, and merciful father which haste compassion of al men, and hate nothing that thou haste made: which would not the death of a sinner, but that he should rather turn from sin, and be saved: mercifully forgeve us our trespasses, and comfort us, which be grieved and wearied [wearied] with the burden of our sin. Thy property is to have mercy, to the only it appertains to forgeve sins: spare us therefore good Lord, spare thy people whom thou haste redeemed. Enter not into judgement with thy servauntes, which be vile earth, and miserable sinners, but so turn thine ire [ire] from us which mekely knowledge [=acknowledge] our vileness, and truly repent us of our faults: so make haste to help us in this world, that we may ever live with thee in the world to come, through Jesus Christ our Lord. Amen.

Then shall the people say this that follows after the Minister.

TURN thou us, O good Lord, and so shall we be turned: be favourable O Lord bee favourable too thy people, which turn to the, in weeping, fasting, and praying, for thou art a merciful God, full of compassion, lunge suffering, and of a great pity. Thou sparest when we deserve punishment, and in thy wrath think upon mercy, spare thy people good Lord, spare them, and let not thy heritage be brought to confusion: hear us O Lord for thy mercy is great, and after the multitude of thy mercies, loke upon us.



Psal. li.
