Â¶ THE ORDER FOR THE

VISITATION OF THE SICK.



The Priest entering into the sick persons house, shall say.

Peace be in* this house, and to all that dwell in it.

When he comes into the sick man presence, he shall say knelynge down.

REMEMBER not Lord our iniquities, nor the iniquities of our forefathers. Spare us good Lord, spare thy people, whom thou hast redeemed with thy most precious blood and bee not angry with us for ever.

Lord have mercy upon us.

Christ have mercy upon us.

Lord have mercy upon us.

Â¶ Our father which art in heaven. &c

And lead us not into temptation.

Answer. But deliver us from evel. Amen.

Â¶ Minister. O Lord save thy servant.

Â¶ Answer. Which puts his trust in the.

Â¶ Answer. And evermore mightily defend him.

Â¶ Minister,

O Lord loke down from Heaven, behold, visit, and relive this thy servant. Loke upon him with the eyes of thy mercy, geve him comfort and sure confidence in the, defend him from the danger of the enemy, and keep him in perpetual peace, and safety: Through Jesus Christ our Lord. Amen.

HEAR us almighty, and most merciful God, and saviour, extend thy accustomed goodness, to this thy servant which is greved with sickness, visit him O Lord, as thou did visit Peters wives mother, and the capiteines servant. So visit and restore unto this sick person his former health (if it bee thy will) or else geve him grace so to take thy visitation, that after this painful life ended, he may dwell with the in life everlasting. Amen.

Â¶ Then shall the Minister exhort the sick person after this form or other like.





* "to" in early 1600's.



DEARLY beloved know this, that almighty god is the lord of life and death, and over al things to them pertaining, as youth, strength, helthe, age weakness, and sickness, wherefore, whatsoever your sickness is, know you certainly, that it is Gods visitation. And for what cause soever this sickness is sent unto you: whether it bee to try your patience for the example of other, and that your faith may be found in the dai of the lord laudable, glorious, and honourable, to the increase of Glory, and endless felicity: Or else it be sent unto you, to correct, and amend in you whatsoever doth offend the eyes of our heavenly father: know you certainly, that if you truly repent you of your sins, and bear your sickness patiently, trusting in Gods mercy for his dere son Jesus Christ's sake, and rendre unto him humble thanks for his fatherly visitation, submitting your self wholly to his will, it shall turn to your profit, and help you forward in the right way that leads unto everlasting life*. Take therefore in good worth, the chastemente of the lord, for whom the lord loves he chastises. yea, as S. Paul saith, he scourges every son which he receives : If you endure chastisement, he offers himself unto you as unto his own children. What son is he that the father chastises not? If ye be not under correction (whereof all true children are partakers) then are ye bastards, and not children. Therefore saying, that when our carnal fathers do correct us, we reverently obey them, shall we not now much rather be obedient to our spiritual father, and so live? And they for a few days do chastise us after their own pleasure, but he doth chastise us for our profit to the intent he may make us partakers of his holiness. These words good brother, are Gods words, and written in holy Scripture for our comfort and instruction, that we should patiently and with thankesgeving, bear our heavenly fathers Correction, whenever by any manner of adversity it shall please his gracious goodness to visit us. And there should be no greater comfort to christian persons, than to be made like unto christ, by suffering patiently adversities, troubles, and Sickenesses. For he him self went not up to joy, but first he suffered pain : hee entered not into his glory, before he was crucified: So truly our way to eternal joy, is to suffer here with Christ, and our door to entry into eternal life: is gladly to die with Christ, that we may rise again from death and dwell with him in everlasting life. Now therefore, taking your sickness, which is thus profitable for you patiently: I exhort you in the name of God, to rernembre the profession which you made unto God, in your Baptism. And forasmuch as after this life there is account [account] to be given unto the rightuous judge, of whom all must be judged without respect of persons: I require you to examine your self and your state, both toward God and man, so that accusing and condempning your self for your own faults, you may find mercy at our heavenly fathers hand, for Christ's sake, and not be accused and condemned in that fearful judgement. Therefore I shall shortly rehearse the Articles of our faith, that ye may know whether you do believe as a Christian man should, or no.

Â¶ Here the minister shall rekerse the articles of the faith saying thus DOEST thou believe in God the father almighty.

And so furs, as it is in Baptism.

1559:





*If the person visited be very sick then the Curate may end his exhortacion in this place.



Â¶	Then shall the minister examine whether he be in charity, with all the world: exhorting him to forgive from the bottom of his hart, al persons that have offended him, and if he have offended other, to ask them forgiveness; And where he has done injury or wrong to any man, that he make amends to the uttermost of his power. And if he have not before disposed his goods, let him the make his will. (But men must be oft admonished that they set an order for their temporal goods and lands,when they be in health.) And also declare his debts, what hee owes, and what is owing unto him, for discharging of his conscience, and quietness ofhis executors. The minister may not forget, nor omit to move the sick person (and that most earnestly) to liberality lowarde the poor.

This may be done before the minister begin his prayers as he shall se cause.



Â¶	Then shall the minister examine whether he be in charity, with all the world, exhorting him to forgive from the bottom of his heart all persons that have offended him, and if he have offended other, to ask them forgiveness: and where hee hath done injury or wrong to any man, that he make amends to the uttermost of his power. And if he have not before disposed his goods, let him the make his will, and also declare his debts, what he owes, and what is owing unto him, for discharging of his conscience, and quietness of his Executors. But men must be oft admonished that they set an order for their temporal goods and lands, when they be in health.

Â¶	These words before rehearsed, may bee said before the Minister begin his prayer, as he shall see cause.

Â¶	The minister may not forget, nor omit to move the sick person (and that most earnestly) to liberality loward the poor.

Â¶	Here shall the sick person make a special confession, if he feel his conscience troubled with any weighty matter. After which confession the priest shall absolve him after this sort.

OUR Lord Jesus Christ who hath left power to his Church to absolve all sinners, which truly repent, and believe in him: of his great mercy forgeve thine offences, and by his authority committed to me, I absolve the from al thy sins. In the name of the father and of the son &c. Amen.

Â¶ And then the priest shall say the Collect following.

Â¶ Let us pray.

O MOST merciful God, which according to the multitude of thy mercies, dost so put away the sins of those which truly repent, that thou remebrest them no more, open thy eye of mercy upon this thy servant, who most earnestly desires pardon, and forgiveness. Renew in him most lovying father, whatsoever hath been decayed, by the fraud, and malice of the devil, or by his own carnal will, and frailnes, preserve, and continue this sick membre in the unity of thy church, consider his contricion, accept his tears, assuage his pain, as shall be scene to thee most expedient for him. And forasmuch as he puts his full trust only in thy mercy, impute not unto him his former sins, but take him to thy favour, through the merits of thy most dearly beloved son Jesus Chriest. Amen.

Â¶ Then the Minister shall say this Psalm.





IN the, O Lord have I put my trust, let me never bee put to confusion, but rid me, and deliver me into thy ryghtuousnesse, incline thine ear unto me and save me.

Be thou my strong hold whereunto I may always resort: thou hast promised to help me, for thou art my house of defence, and my Castle.

Deliver me a my God out of the hand of the ungodly: out of the hand of the unrightuous and cruel man.

For thou O lord God art the thing that I long for : thou art my hope even from my youth.

Through the have I ben holden up ever sense I was borne: thou art he that toke me out of my mothers womb, my praise shall always be of the.

I am become as it were a monster unto many: but my sure trust is in the.

O let my mouth be filled with thy praise: (that I may sing of thy glory) and honour all the day lunge.

Cast me not away in the time of age: forsake me not when my strength fails me.

For mine enemies speak against me, and they that lay wait for my soul, take their counsel together, saiynge: God hath forsaken him, persecute him, and take him, for there is none to deliver him.

Go not far from me, O God: my God, haste the to help me.

Let them be confounded and perish, that are against my soul: let them be covered with shame and dishonour that seek to do me evil.

As for me, I will pacietly abide always : and will praise the, more and more.

My mouth shall daily speak of thy righteousness, and salvation: for I know no end thereof.

I will go furs in the strength of the Lord God: and will make mention of thy righteousness only.

Thou (O God) haste taught me from my youth up until now: therefore I will tell of thy wondrous works.

Forsake me not (O God) in mine old age, when I am gray headed: until I have showed thy strength unto this generation, and thy power to all them that are yet for to come.

Thy righteousness (O God) is very high, and great things are they that thou haste done: O God, who is like unto the?

O what great troubles and adversities hast thou showed me? and yet did thou turn and refresh me, yea, and brought me from the deep of the earth again.

Thou hast brought me to great honour: and comforted me on every side.

Therefore will I praise the and thy faythefulnes (O God) plaiynge upon an instrument of Music: unto the will I singe upon the Harp, O thou holy one of Israel.

My lips will be fine, when I sing unto the: and so will my soul whom thou hast delivered.

My tongue also shall talk of thy righteousness al the day long : for they are confounded and brought unto shame, that seek to do me evil.

Glory be to the Father, and to the Son, and to the holy Ghost.

As it was in the beginning, is now and ever shall be world without end. Amen.

Adding this.

O SAVIOUR of the world, save us, which by thy cross and precious blood hast redeemed us, help us we beseech the, O God.

Â¶ Then shall the Minister say.

THE almighty Lord; which is a most strong tower to all them that put their trust in him, to whom all things in heaven, in earth, and under the earth doe bow and obey, be now; and evermore thy defence, and make the know and feel, that there is no other name under heaven given to man, in whom, and through whom thou may receive health and salvation, but only .the name of our Lord Jesus Christ. Amen.

In te, domino, spe. Psal. lxxi.





Â¶ THE



COMMUNION OF THE SICK.

Forasmuch as al mortal men be subject to many soubdein perils, diseases, and sicknesses, and ever uncertain what time they shall departs out of this lyf. Therefore to the intent they may be always in a readiness to die, whenever it that please Almighty God to cal them: The Curates shall diligently from time to time, but specially in the plague time, exhort their Parishioners to the oft receiving in the Church, of the holy Communion of the body and blood of our saviour Christ. Which (if they do) they shall have no cause in their soubdeine visitation to be unquieted for lacks of the same. But if the sick persons be not able to come to the Church, and yet is desirous to receive the Communion in his house, then ye must give knowledge over night, or else early in the Morning to the Curate, signifying also how many be appointed to communicate with him. And havyng a convenient place in the sick mans house, where the Curate may reverently minister, and a good number to receive the Communion with the sick persons, with all things necessary for the same, he that there minister the holy Communion.

The Collect.

ALMIGHTY everlivyng God, maker of mankind, which doest correct those whom thou doest love, and chastisest every one whom thou doest receive, we beseech the to have mercy upon this thy servant visited with thy hand, and to grant that he may take his sickness patiently, and recover his bodily health (if it be thy gracious will), and whenever his soul shall depart from the body, it may bee without spot presented unto the: Through Jesus Christ our Lord. Amen.





The Epistle.

MY son, despise not the correction of the Lord, neither faint when thou art rebuked of him. For whom the Lord loves, him he corrects : yea, and he scourges every son whom he receives.





Hebr. xii.



The Gospel.

VERILY, verily I say unto you, he that hears my word, and beleveth on him that sent me, hath everlasting life, and shall not come unto dampnacion, but he passes from death unto life.

Â¶	At the time of the distribution of the holy Sacrament, the Priest shall flrst receive the Communion himself, and after minister unto them that be appointed to communicate with the sick.

Â¶	But if any man, either by reason of extremity of sickness, or for lack of warning in due time to the Curate, or for lack of company to receive with him, or by any other just impediment, do not receive the Sacrament of Christ's body and blood, then the Curate shall instruct him, that if he do truly repent him of his sins, and steadfastly believe that Jesus Christ hath sufred death upon the cross for him, and shed his blood for his redempcion, earnestly remembering the benefits he hath thereby, and giving him hearty thanks therefore, he doth eat and drink the body and blonde of our saviour Christ, profitably to his souls health, although he doe not receive the Sacrament with his mouth.

Â¶	When the sick person is visited, and receives the holy Communion al at one time, then the Priest, for more expedition, shall cut of the form of the visitation at the Psaime, In the, O Lord have I put my trust, and go straight to the Communion.

Â¶	In the time of plague, Sweat, or such other like contagious times of sickenesses or diseases, when none of the Paroshe or neighbours can be gotten to communicate with the sick in their houses, for fear of the infection, upon special request of the diseased, the minister may alonly communicate with him.

The collects and Bible readings for Holy Communion in the 1549, 1552, and 1559 Books of Common Prayer are, with some small exceptions, all identical among those three editions, and so are all given here together. The major difference is that only the 1549 Book has the Introit (or Psalm) appointed for each Sunday and Holy Day; this is omitted in the other books. Also, only the 1549 book has readings appointed for Matins (Morning Prayer) and Evensong (Evening Prayer) for certain Sundays and Holy Days; these are given in the Calendar for the other books.

The translation used is that of the Great Bible (a portion of which is pictured below), the first authorized English translation. This translation, compiled by Miles Coverdale, was closely based on the very first printed English translation, that of Tyndale. While the Epistles and Gospels were replaced by the "Authorized", or King James version for the 1662 Book of Common Prayer, the Psalms given here, as translated by Coverdale, continued to be used in all editions of the Book of Common Prayer through the U. S. 1928 edition.
